Also note that only one instance of a particular\n    39→/// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\n    40→/// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\n    41→/// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n    42→/// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n    43→/// free'd.\n    44→///\n    45→class Type {\n    46→public:\n    47→  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n    48→  /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n    49→  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n    50→  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n    51→  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n    52→  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n    53→  ///\n    54→  enum TypeID {\n    55→    // PrimitiveTypes\n    56→    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    57→    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    58→    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    59→    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    60→    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    61→    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    62→    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    63→    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    64→    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    65→    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    66→    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    67→    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n    68→\n    69→    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    70→    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    71→    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    72→    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    73→    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    74→    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    75→    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    76→    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    77→    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    78→    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n    79→  };\n    80→\n    81→private:\n    82→  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n    83→  LLVMContext &Context;\n    84→\n    85→  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n    86→  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n    87→                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n    88→                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n    89→\n    90→protected:\n    91→  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n    92→\n    93→  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    94→    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n    95→  ~Type() = default;\n    96→\n    97→  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; For example, this\n   109→  /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\n   110→  /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\n   111→  /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\n   112→  /// Float).\n   113→  Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\n   114→\n   115→public:\n   116→  /// Print the current type.\n   117→  /// Omit the type details if \\p NoDetails == true.\n   118→  /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\n   119→  /// When \\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\n   120→  /// Put differently, \\p NoDetails prints the type as if\n   121→  /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\n   122→  LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\n   123→                      bool NoDetails = false) const;\n   124→\n   125→  LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n   126→\n   127→  /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n   128→  LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\n   129→\n   130→  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n   131→  // Accessors for working with types.\n   132→  //\n   133→\n   134→  /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\n   135→  /// elements defined above.\n   136→  TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\n   137→\n   138→  /// Return true if this is 'void'.\n   139→  bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; For more \"Type\"\n// stuff, look in DerivedTypes.h.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_TYPE_H\n#define LLVM_IR_TYPE_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/ArrayRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/CBindingWrapping.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Casting.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/ErrorHandling.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n#include <iterator>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass IntegerType;\nstruct fltSemantics;\nclass LLVMContext;\nclass PointerType;\nclass raw_ostream;\nclass StringRef;\ntemplate <typename PtrType> class SmallPtrSetImpl;\n\n/// The instances of the Type class are immutable: once they are created,\n/// they are never changed.  Also note that only one instance of a particular\n/// type is ever created.  Thus seeing if two types are equal is a matter of\n/// doing a trivial pointer comparison. To enforce that no two equal instances\n/// are created, Type instances can only be created via static factory methods\n/// in class Type and in derived classes.  Once allocated, Types are never\n/// free'd.\n///\nclass Type {\npublic:\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\n  /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\n  /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\n  /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\n  /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\n  ///\n  enum TypeID {\n    // PrimitiveTypes\n    HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\n    BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\n    FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\n    DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\n    X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\n    FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\n    PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\n    VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\n    LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\n    MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\n    X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\n    TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\n\n    // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\n    IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\n    FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\n    PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\n    StructTyID,         ///< Structures\n    ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\n    FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\n    ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\n    TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\n    TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\n  };\n\nprivate:\n  /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &Context;\n\n  TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\n  unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\n                              // Note that this should be synchronized with\n                              // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\n\nprotected:\n  friend class LLVMContextImpl;\n\n  explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\n    : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\n  ~Type() = default;\n\n  unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; }\n\n  void setSubclassData(unsigned val) {\n    SubclassData = val;\n    // Ensure we don't have any accidental truncation.\n    assert(getSubclassData() == val && \"Subclass data too large for field\");\n  }\n\n  /// Keeps track of how many Type*'s there are in the ContainedTys list.\n  unsigned NumContainedTys = 0;\n\n  /// A pointer to the array of Types contained by this Type. For example, this\n  /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\n  /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\n  /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\n  /// Float).\n  Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\n\npublic:\n  /// Print the current type.\n  /// Omit the type details if \\p NoDetails == true.\n  /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\n  /// When \\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\n  /// Put differently, \\p NoDetails prints the type as if\n  /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\n  LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\n                      bool NoDetails = false) const;\n\n  LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\n\n  /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\n  LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Accessors for working with types.\n  //\n\n  /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\n  /// elements defined above.\n  TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'void'.\n  bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'half', a 16-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isHalfTy() const { return getTypeID() == HalfTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'bfloat', a 16-bit bfloat type.\n  bool isBFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a 16-bit float type.\n  bool is16bitFPTy() const {\n    return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID || getTypeID() == HalfTyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'float', a 32-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == FloatTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'double', a 64-bit IEEE fp type.\n  bool isDoubleTy() const { return getTypeID() == DoubleTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is x86 long double.\n  bool isX86_FP80Ty() const { return getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is 'fp128'.\n  bool isFP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == FP128TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is powerpc long double.\n  bool isPPC_FP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a well-behaved IEEE-like type, which has a IEEE\n  /// compatible layout, and does not have non-IEEE values, such as x86_fp80's\n  /// unnormal values.\n  bool isIEEELikeFPTy() const {\n    switch (getTypeID()) {\n    case DoubleTyID:\n    case FloatTyID:\n    case HalfTyID:\n    case BFloatTyID:\n    case FP128TyID:\n      return true;\n    default:\n      return false;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is one of the floating-point types\n  bool isFloatingPointTy() const {\n    return isIEEELikeFPTy() || getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID ||\n           getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Returns true if this is a floating-point type that is an unevaluated sum\n  /// of multiple floating-point units.\n  /// An example of such a type is ppc_fp128, also known as double-double, which\n  /// consists of two IEEE 754 doubles.\n  bool isMultiUnitFPType() const {\n    return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\n  }\n\n  LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is X86 AMX.\n  bool isX86_AMXTy() const { return getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a target extension type.\n  bool isTargetExtTy() const { return getTypeID() == TargetExtTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a target extension type with a scalable layout.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTargetExtTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is a type whose size is a known multiple of vscale.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool isScalableTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n  /// disallows being used as a global.\n  LLVM_ABI bool\n  containsNonGlobalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonGlobalTargetExtType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is or contains a target extension type that\n  /// disallows being used as a local.\n  LLVM_ABI bool\n  containsNonLocalTargetExtType(SmallPtrSetImpl<const Type *> &Visited) const;\n  LLVM_ABI bool containsNonLocalTargetExtType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is a FP type or a vector of FP.\n  bool isFPOrFPVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isFloatingPointTy(); }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an IntegerType of the given width.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isIntegerTy(unsigned Bitwidth) const;\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types.\n  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(); }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a vector of integer types of\n  /// the given width.\n  bool isIntOrIntVectorTy(unsigned BitWidth) const {\n    return getScalarType()->isIntegerTy(BitWidth);\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is an integer type or a pointer type.\n  bool isIntOrPtrTy() const { return isIntegerTy() || isPointerTy(); }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of FunctionType.\n  bool isFunctionTy() const { return getTypeID() == FunctionTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of StructType.\n  bool isStructTy() const { return getTypeID() == StructTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of ArrayType.\n  bool isArrayTy() const { return getTypeID() == ArrayTyID; }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of PointerType.\n  bool isPointerTy() const { return getTypeID() == PointerTyID; }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a pointer type or a vector of pointer types.\n  bool isPtrOrPtrVectorTy() const { return getScalarType()->isPointerTy(); }\n\n  /// True if this is an instance of VectorType.\n  inline bool isVectorTy() const {\n    return getTypeID() == ScalableVectorTyID || getTypeID() == FixedVectorTyID;\n  }\n\n  // True if this is an instance of TargetExtType of RISC-V vector tuple.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isRISCVVectorTupleTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type could be converted with a lossless BitCast to\n  /// type 'Ty'. For example, i8* to i32*. BitCasts are valid for types of the\n  /// same size only where no re-interpretation of the bits is done.\n  /// Determine if this type could be losslessly bitcast to Ty\n  LLVM_ABI bool canLosslesslyBitCastTo(Type *Ty) const;\n\n  /// Return true if this type is empty, that is, it has no elements or all of\n  /// its elements are empty.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isEmptyTy() const;\n\n  /// Return true if the type is \"first class\", meaning it is a valid type for a\n  /// Value.\n  LLVM_ABI bool isFirstClassType() const;\n\n  /// Return true if the type is a valid type for a register in codegen. This\n  /// includes all first-class types except struct and array types.\n  bool isSingleValueType() const {\n    return isFloatingPointTy() || isIntegerTy() || isPointerTy() ||\n           isVectorTy() || isX86_AMXTy() || isTargetExtTy();\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if the type is an aggregate type. This means it is valid as\n  /// the first operand of an insertvalue or extractvalue instruction. This\n  /// includes struct and array types, but does not include vector types.\n  bool isAggregateType() const {\n    return getTypeID() == StructTyID || getTypeID() == ArrayTyID;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if it makes sense to take the size of this type. To get the\n  /// actual size for a particular target, it is reasonable to use the\n  /// DataLayout subsystem to do this.\n  bool isSized(SmallPtrSetImpl<Type*> *Visited = nullptr) const {\n    // If it's a primitive, it is always sized.\n    if (getTypeID() == IntegerTyID || isFloatingPointTy() ||\n        getTypeID() == PointerTyID || getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID)\n      return true;\n    // If it is not something that can have a size (e.g. a function or label),\n    // it doesn't have a size.\n    if (getTypeID() != StructTyID && getTypeID() != ArrayTyID &&\n        !isVectorTy() && getTypeID() != TargetExtTyID)\n      return false;\n    // Otherwise we have to try harder to decide.\n    return isSizedDerivedType(Visited);\n  }\n\n  /// Return the basic size of this type if it is a primitive type. These are\n  /// fixed by LLVM and are not target-dependent.\n  /// This will return zero if the type does not have a size or is not a\n  /// primitive type.\n  ///\n  /// If this is a scalable vector type, the scalable property will be set and\n  /// the runtime size will be a positive integer multiple of the base size.\n  ///\n  /// Note that this may not reflect the size of memory allocated for an\n  /// instance of the type or the number of bytes that are written when an\n  /// instance of the type is stored to memory. The DataLayout class provides\n  /// additional query functions to provide this information.\n  ///\n  LLVM_ABI TypeSize getPrimitiveSizeInBits() const LLVM_READONLY;\n\n  /// If this is a vector type, return the getPrimitiveSizeInBits value for the\n  /// element type. Otherwise return the getPrimitiveSizeInBits value for this\n  /// type.\n  LLVM_ABI unsigned getScalarSizeInBits() const LLVM_READONLY;\n\n  /// Return the width of the mantissa of this type. If the FP type does not have a stable mantissa (e.g.\n  /// ppc long double), this method returns -1.\n  LLVM_ABI int getFPMantissaWidth() const;\n\n  /// If this is a vector type, return the element type, otherwise return\n  /// 'this'.\n  inline Type *getScalarType() const {\n    if (isVectorTy())\n      return getContainedType(0);\n    return const_cast<Type *>(this);\n  }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Type Iteration support.\n  //\n  using subtype_iterator = Type * const *;\n\n  subtype_iterator subtype_begin() const { return ContainedTys; }\n  subtype_iterator subtype_end() const { return &ContainedTys[NumContainedTys];}\n  ArrayRef<Type*> subtypes() const {\n    return ArrayRef(subtype_begin(), subtype_end());\n  }\n\n  using subtype_reverse_iterator = std::reverse_iterator<subtype_iterator>;\n\n  subtype_reverse_iterator subtype_rbegin() const {\n    return subtype_reverse_iterator(subtype_end());\n  }\n  subtype_reverse_iterator subtype_rend() const {\n    return subtype_reverse_iterator(subtype_begin());\n  }\n\n  /// This method is used to implement the type iterator (defined at the end of\n  /// the file). For derived types, this returns the types 'contained' in the\n  /// derived type.\n  Type *getContainedType(unsigned i) const {\n    assert(i < NumContainedTys && \"Index out of range!\");\n    return ContainedTys[i];\n  }\n\n  /// Return the number of types in the derived type.\n  unsigned getNumContainedTypes() const { return NumContainedTys; }\n\n  //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n  // Helper methods corresponding to subclass methods. These are things like \"arrays of x\" or \"structure of x, y, z\" or\n// \"function returning x taking (y,z) as parameters\", etc...\n//\n// The implementations of these classes live in the Type.cpp file.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_IR_DERIVEDTYPES_H\n#define LLVM_IR_DERIVEDTYPES_H\n\n#include \"llvm/ADT/ArrayRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/STLExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/StringRef.h\"\n#include \"llvm/IR/Type.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Casting.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\nclass Value;\nclass APInt;\nclass LLVMContext;\ntemplate <typename T> class Expected;\nclass Error;\n\n/// Class to represent integer types. This is a private interface\n// shared between the code that implements the SelectionDAG::LegalizeTypes\n// method.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n#define LLVM_LIB_CODEGEN_SELECTIONDAG_LEGALIZETYPES_H\n\n#include \"MatchContext.h\"\n#include \"llvm/ADT/DenseMap.h\"\n#include \"llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h\"\n#include \"llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n/// This takes an arbitrary SelectionDAG as input and hacks on it until only\n/// value types the target machine can handle are left. This involves promoting\n/// small sizes to large sizes or splitting up large values into small values.\n///\nclass LLVM_LIBRARY_VISIBILITY DAGTypeLegalizer {\n  const TargetLowering &TLI;\n  SelectionDAG &DAG;\npublic:\n  /// This pass uses the NodeId on the SDNodes to hold information about the\n  /// state of the node. The enum has all the values.\n  enum NodeIdFlags {\n    /// All operands have been processed, so this node is ready to be handled.\n    ReadyToProcess = 0,\n\n    /// This is a new node, not before seen, that was created in the process of\n    /// legalizing some other node.\n    NewNode = -1,\n\n    /// This node's ID needs to be set to the number of its unprocessed\n    /// operands.\n    Unanalyzed = -2,\n\n    /// This is a node that has already been processed.\n    Processed = -3\n\n    // 1+ - This is a node which has this many unprocessed operands.\n  };\nprivate:\n\n  /// This is a bitvector that contains two bits for each simple value type,\n  /// where the two bits correspond to the LegalizeAction enum from\n  /// TargetLowering. This can be queried with \"getTypeAction(VT)\".\n  TargetLowering::ValueTypeActionImpl ValueTypeActions;\n\n  /// Return how we should legalize values of this type.\n  TargetLowering::LegalizeTypeAction getTypeAction(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT);\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this type is legal on this target.\n  bool isTypeLegal(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT) == TargetLowering::TypeLegal;\n  }\n\n  /// Return true if this is a simple legal type.\n  bool isSimpleLegalType(EVT VT) const {\n    return VT.isSimple() && TLI.isTypeLegal(VT);\n  }\n\n  EVT getSetCCResultType(EVT VT) const {\n    return TLI.getSetCCResultType(DAG.getDataLayout(), *DAG.getContext(), VT);\n  }\n\n  /// Pretend all of this node's results are legal.\n  bool IgnoreNodeResults(SDNode *N) const {\n    return N->getOpcode() == ISD::TargetConstant ||\n           N->getOpcode() == ISD::Register;\n  }\n\n  // Bijection from SDValue to unique id. As each created node gets a\n  // new id we do not need to worry about reuse expunging.  Should we\n  // run out of ids, we can do a one time expensive compactifcation.\n  typedef unsigned TableId;\n\n  TableId NextValueId = 1;\n\n  SmallDenseMap<SDValue, TableId, 8> ValueToIdMap;\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, SDValue, 8> IdToValueMap;\n\n  /// For integer nodes that are below legal width, this map indicates what\n  /// promoted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedIntegers;\n\n  /// For integer nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which\n  /// operands are the expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedIntegers;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes converted to integers of the same size, this map\n  /// indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftenedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates what promoted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedFloats;\n\n  /// For floating-point nodes that have a smaller precision than the smallest\n  /// supported precision, this map indicates the converted value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> SoftPromotedHalfs;\n\n  /// For float nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which operands\n  /// are the expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> ExpandedFloats;\n\n  /// For nodes that are <1 x ty>, this map indicates the scalar value of type\n  /// 'ty' to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ScalarizedVectors;\n\n  /// For nodes that need to be split this map indicates which operands are the\n  /// expanded version of the input.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, std::pair<TableId, TableId>, 8> SplitVectors;\n\n  /// For vector nodes that need to be widened, indicates the widened value to\n  /// use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> WidenedVectors;\n\n  /// For values that have been replaced with another, indicates the replacement\n  /// value to use.\n  SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> ReplacedValues;\n\n  /// This defines a worklist of nodes to process. This allows the target specific behavior\n// of instructions to be described to target independent passes.\n//\n//===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n\n#ifndef LLVM_CODEGEN_VALUETYPES_H\n#define LLVM_CODEGEN_VALUETYPES_H\n\n#include \"llvm/CodeGenTypes/MachineValueType.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/Compiler.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/MathExtras.h\"\n#include \"llvm/Support/TypeSize.h\"\n#include <cassert>\n#include <cstdint>\n#include <string>\n\nnamespace llvm {\n\n  class LLVMContext;\n  class Type;\n  struct fltSemantics;\n\n  /// Extended Value Type. Capable of holding value types which are not native\n  /// for any processor (such as the i12345 type), as well as the types an MVT\n  /// can represent.\n  struct EVT {\n  private:\n    MVT V = MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;\n    Type *LLVMTy = nullptr;\n\n  public:\n    constexpr EVT() = default;\n    constexpr EVT(MVT::SimpleValueType SVT) : V(SVT) {}\n    constexpr EVT(MVT S) : V(S) {}\n\n    bool operator==(EVT VT) const {\n      return !(*this != VT);\n    }\n    bool operator!=(EVT VT) const {\n      if (V.SimpleTy != VT.V.SimpleTy)\n        return true;\n      if (V.SimpleTy == MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return LLVMTy != VT.LLVMTy;\n      return false;\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a floating-point type with the given\n    /// number of bits. There are two floating-point types with 128 bits - this\n    /// returns f128 rather than ppcf128.\n    static EVT getFloatingPointVT(unsigned BitWidth) {\n      return MVT::getFloatingPointVT(BitWidth);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents an integer with the given number of\n    /// bits.\n    static EVT getIntegerVT(LLVMContext &Context, unsigned BitWidth) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getIntegerVT(BitWidth);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedIntegerVT(Context, BitWidth);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector NumElements in length, where\n    /// each element is of type VT.\n    static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, unsigned NumElements,\n                           bool IsScalable = false) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, NumElements, IsScalable);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedVectorVT(Context, VT, NumElements, IsScalable);\n    }\n\n    /// Returns the EVT that represents a vector EC.Min elements in length,\n    /// where each element is of type VT.\n    static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, ElementCount EC) {\n      MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(VT.V, EC);\n      if (M.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n        return M;\n      return getExtendedVectorVT(Context, VT, EC);\n    }\n\n    /// Return a vector with the same number of elements as this vector, but\n    /// with the element type converted to an integer type with the same\n    /// bitwidth.\n    EVT changeVectorElementTypeToInteger() const {\n      if (isSimple())\n        return getSimpleVT().changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n      return changeExtendedVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for a vector type whose attributes match ourselves\n    /// with the exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n    EVT changeVectorElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n      if (isSimple() && EltVT.isSimple()) {\n        MVT M = MVT::getVectorVT(EltVT.getSimpleVT(), getVectorElementCount());\n        if (M != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE)\n          return M;\n      }\n      return getVectorVT(Context, EltVT, getVectorElementCount());\n    }\n\n    /// Return a VT for a type whose attributes match ourselves with the\n    /// exception of the element type that is chosen by the caller.\n    EVT changeElementType(LLVMContext &Context, EVT EltVT) const {\n      EltVT = EltVT.getScalarType();\n      return isVector() ? changeVectorElementType(Context, EltVT) : EltVT;\n    }\n\n    /// Return the type converted to an equivalently sized integer or vector\n    /// with integer element type. Similar to changeVectorElementTypeToInteger,\n    /// but also handles scalars.\n    EVT changeTypeToInteger() const {\n      if (isVector())\n        return changeVectorElementTypeToInteger();\n\n      if (isSimple())\n        return getSimpleVT().changeTypeToInteger();\n      return changeExtendedTypeToInteger();\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT has zero size, this will fail if called on a\n    /// scalable type\n    bool isZeroSized() const {\n      return getSizeInBits().isZero();\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT is simple (as opposed to being extended).\n    bool isSimple() const {\n      return V.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;\n    }\n\n    /// Test if the given EVT is extended (as opposed to being simple).\n    bool isExtended() const {\n      return !isSimple();\n    }\n\n    /// Return true if this is a FP or a vector FP type.\n    bool isFloatingPoint() const {\n      return isSimple() ? V.isFloatingPoint() : isExtendedFloatingPoint();\n    }\n","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":574}}}

generation through several well-defined stages:\\n\\n**Stage 1: LLVM IR Type Class Hierarchy**\\nThe foundation is the Type class (llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h) which serves as the base for all LLVM types. It defines an enum TypeID containing all type classifications (IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, StructTyID, etc.). Derived type classes are declared in llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h:\\n- IntegerType: Represents arbitrary-precision integers (class IntegerType : public Type)\\n- FunctionType: Represents function signatures with return type and parameters\\n- StructType: Represents named and literal structure types, supporting both packed and unpacked layouts\\n- ArrayType, VectorType, PointerType: Additional derived types for complex data structures\\n\\n**Stage 2: Context Ownership and Type Uniquing**\\nAll Type instances are owned and uniqued by the LLVMContext (llvm/include/llvm/IR/LLVMContext.h). The public LLVMContext class maintains a pointer to LLVMContextImpl (llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h), which is the opaque implementation containing:\\n- Type uniquing tables (IntegerTypes map, FunctionTypes folding set, StructTypes folding set)\\n- AnonStructTypeKeyInfo, FunctionTypeKeyInfo, TargetExtTypeKeyInfo for type hashing and comparison\\nType creation methods like IntegerType::get() in llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp check these tables: `IntegerType *&Entry = C.pImpl->IntegerTypes[NumBits]; if (!Entry) Entry = new (C.pImpl->Alloc) IntegerType(C, NumBits);`\\n\\n**Stage 3: IR Types to Machine Types (EVT)**\\nThe conversion from LLVM IR types to machine-level types occurs through the ValueTypes system (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h). EVT (Extended Value Type) is a hybrid type that can represent both:\\n- Simple machine value types (MVT) for common types like i32, f64, v4i32\\n- Extended types pointing back to LLVM IR types for non-standard sizes\\n\\nThe key conversion method TargetLowering::getValueType() (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h:1740) converts LLVM types to EVT:\\n- For PointerType: calls getPointerTy(DL, AddressSpace)\\n- For VectorType: recursively converts element types and calls EVT::getVectorVT()\\n- For other types: calls EVT::getEVT(Ty)\\n\\nEVT::getEVT() in llvm/lib/CodeGen/ValueTypes.cpp (line 301) performs the actual conversion:\\n- TokenTyID → MVT::Untyped\\n- IntegerTyID → getIntegerVT(BitWidth) - creates extended integer types for non-standard widths\\n- FixedVectorTyID/ScalableVectorTyID → getVectorVT() - recursively converts element types\\n\\n**Stage 4: SelectionDAG IR-to-DAG Conversion**\\nSelectionDAGBuilder (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.h and .cpp) traverses the LLVM IR and creates a SelectionDAG (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h) with SDNode values of EVT types. The builder calls TLI.getValueType() to determine the appropriate machine type for each IR value.\\n\\n**Stage 5: Type Legalization**\\nDAGTypeLegalizer (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h and .cpp) transforms the DAG to ensure all value types are legal for the target. It:\\n- Queries TargetLowering::getTypeAction() to determine how to handle each EVT\\n- Promotes small types (e.g., i8 → i32), expands large types (e.g., i128 → two i64s), or leaves them legal\\n- Maintains maps (PromotedIntegers, ExpandedIntegers, SplitVectors, WidenedVectors) tracking transformations\\n\\n**Stage 6: Instruction Selection**\\nSelectionDAGISel (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAGISel.h and .cpp) converts the legalized DAG to machine instructions by matching target-specific patterns. The MVT from the legalized DAG nodes determines which machine instructions are selected.\\n\\nThe complete chain demonstrates LLVM's design: IR types provide semantic structure (arbitrary precision integers, function signatures), contexts manage type uniqueness for memory efficiency, EVT bridges IR to target-independent machine concepts, and SelectionDAG+LegalizeTypes adapts to specific target capabilities before final instruction selection.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2140,"cache_read_input_tokens":66909,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2140},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5d3c87de-60db-456a-a82f-205e47bdaf44","uuid":"36521852-2eda-4768-8965-34d02f4d2b6f"}
